Krishnam Vande Jagadgurum

Vasudeva Sutam Devam  
Kamsa Chanoora Mardanam ! 
Devaki Paramaanandam  
Krishnam Vande Jagat Gurum !!

Meaning 

I worship Lord Kṛṣṇa, Who is the spiritual master of the universe, Who is the son of Vasudeva, Who is the Lord, Who killed Kamsa and Cāṇūra, and Who is the bliss of Devakī.

वसुदेवसुतं देवं कंसचाणूरमर्दनम् । 
देवकीपरमानन्दं कृष्णं वंदे जगद्गुरुम् ।।

 @sunainavamshi5961   Thanks to Google:
I am from Sydney :


No, internship and house surgery are not the same. Internship, also known as housemanship or PGY1 training, is the first year of postgraduate training for medical graduates in Australia, while house surgery is not a recognized term in medical training. 

Internship: First year of clinical training after medical school, often focused on broad exposure to different specialties.
Housemanship: A subsequent period of training, often involving more responsibility and independence in patient care.
The usage of these terms can vary by country, so it's important to consider the context in which they are used.

General information.. When you see National Medical Commission & Dental council of India regulations, if you have to practice facial cosmetic procedures or hair transplant procedures in India you have to be a Certified Plastic surgeon or a certified Dermatologist or a certified Maxillofacial surgeon.. Rest all other doctors were not eligible to practice these procedures in India..  So if any clinic have these doctors you can consult them..

Spilling some facts for the unaware-
1) Harshitha did engineering and later took a course in Cosmetology(probably 6months-1yr course). So now she became a cosmetologist(not a dermatologist). Cosmetology is a course which can be taken by anybody (even if you are just 10th pass, or you did Hotel management or engineering or bpharma or you are entirely from a different profession also, you can take up cosmetology course.)
2) As a cosmetologist if you want to start a clinic NOT just for eyebrow colouring or lip colouring but want to treat acne, prescribe medicines, do hair transplantations or similar medical procedures, that should at all costs be under the supervision of a dermatologist (someone who completed MBBS and did PG in Dermatology).
3) Now what actually went wrong with HK clinic is that Harshita claimed herself to be a doctor in her instagram reels by wearing apron and scrubs with her name mentioned on her scrubs as Dr.Harshita. She received a doctorate degree(not a doctor degree!!) from some foreign university and started claiming herself to be a doctor by keeping the prefix Dr before her name. In her case- (Hon) Dr. Harshita should be mentioned instead of Dr.Harshita as there’s head to toe difference between both of them.
4) For all their branches, they have managed to only keep 1 actual dermatologist (there’s solid proof) instead of atleast 1/branch. So doing dermat procedures without doctor supervision is terribly wrong and illegal.
5) Now that ppl are getting aware of all this stuff, she posted a reel saying “Im not a dermat and I dont do any procedures, I just stand there”.
6) Social media these days is influencing ppl so much so that they started believing anything and everything they see. Dont be fools, have basic awareness dear ppl.
The same is the issue with Layers clinic- Dr.Kaumudi is a dentist who later took up cometology course and became a cosmetologist. They too hired only a single dermatologist for all their 7 branches instead of atleast 1/branch, meaning they are doing procedures without any supervision and some other cosmetologists who are prescribing medications which is illegal.
taking into consideration the hefty amounts they charge for each procedure, they shouldn’t play with people’s lives.
Hope this helped anyone who’s unaware of these things.

Ms. Mandava must also acknowledge a fundamental aspect of medical practice: asking about a patient's history — including alcohol use, smoking habits, or sexual activity — is standard and essential across all disciplines. These are not intrusive or inappropriate questions; they are clinical necessities that guide diagnosis and determine safe, effective treatment plans.

In todays context, where substance use and risky behaviors are prevalent among the younger population, it becomes all the more critical for doctors to inquire about such factors with sensitivity and professionalism. If someone feels offended by such questions, it reflects a lack of understanding of how medicine functions — not a fault on the part of the practitioner.

As medical professionals, we are trained to approach these topics with discretion and care. Patients, in turn, must understand that such discussions are integral to their care and safety.

My message for HK clinic 

I’m concerned about the qualifications of the staff at your clinic. The woman who performed my treatment mentioned she had only completed intermediate education, yet she was responsible for procedures that should require specialized dermatological knowledge. During my visit, a dermatologist recommended fillers and Botox, but the person administering the treatment lacked even basic understanding of skincare ingredients like hyaluronic acid or niacinamide. She could only refer to treatments by their color, which suggests a lack of proper training. If this is truly a clinic, only licensed dermatologists should be performing such procedures. Otherwise, it would be more accurate to classify it as a salon.

Good job 👏👏👏
Despite being a well-established and authorized salon, the lack of truly professional staff has become increasingly apparent. Unfortunately, this was my experience at a particular salon (which I prefer not to name). I invested a significant amount in a treatment that did not meet expectations, and it was a disappointing experience—enough for me to decide that I will no longer pursue salon treatments.

The core issue seems to be staffing. When skilled professionals are not offered competitive compensation, it’s understandable that they seek opportunities elsewhere. As a result, salons often resort to hiring untrained or minimally trained individuals and provide only a basic salary. Given the employment landscape in India, there is no shortage of people willing to work for such wages, but this approach severely compromises the quality of service.

Cringe actor.
It’s hard to understand how some actors are still popular in Tollywood. Their acting is almost the same in every movie. Same expressions, same way of talking, and that strange accent—it all feels forced and uncomfortable. Many times, we can’t even understand what they’re saying. They try to do comedy, but it just looks silly and cringe. The worst part? They behave like that in real life too.

What’s more confusing is how the Telugu audience keeps supporting this. Because of that, directors also keep making the same kind of movies again and again. No strong story, no good message—just noise and time pass.

Let’s be honest, the only reason Tollywood got attention recently is because of Baahubali, Pushpa, RRR, and now Kalki. Without those movies, 95% of Telugu films today are not even worth watching. Now look at Malayalam movies—they don’t have big stars or big budgets, but the stories are powerful. People talk about them because the content is real.

Even Tamil movies are doing better. They add some commercial scenes, but still try to tell good stories. Their movies keep us engaged from start to finish.

If you remove Rajamouli and Sukumar, Tollywood would still be where it was 15 years ago.

Take actors like Mahesh Babu, Nithiin, Sharwanand, Nikhil, Naga Chaitanya, Vishwak Sen, Ravi Teja, Ram, Gopichand, Sudheer Babu, Varun Tej etc..—they’ve all done many movies in the last 10 years, but how many of those films were really good? Maybe one or two. Rest are just a waste of time and money.

I’m not an expert. I’m just a Telugu movie fan. But honestly, I feel really disappointed with how most Telugu movies have become. It’s time to focus on real stories and good acting—not just hype.

YouTube లో, news లో, SM లో, కామెంట్స్ పెట్టే వాళ్ళలో ప్రతి ఒక్కరికీ యుద్ధమే కావాలి అందర్నీ చంపెయ్యాలి. ఎవరికి రేపటి గురించి సాధారణ సిటిజన్ గురించి అవసరమే లేదు. మనం ఇండియన్ గవర్నమెంట్ అలా రెస్పాండ్ అవుతుంది ఇలా చిటికెలో లేపెస్తుంది అని చెప్పుకుంటున్నాము గానీ దాడికి పాల్పడిన సంఘటనని దాని మూలాన్ని గుర్తించటం లో మన ఇంటెలిజెన్స్, గవర్నమెంట్ పూర్తిగా ఫెయిల్ అయిందనే విషయం ఎవరు ఒప్పుకోవటం లేదు ప్రశ్నించటం లేదు. ప్రశ్నించే వాళ్ళు మిగతా వాళ్ళకి నచ్చటం లేదు. ప్రశ్నించటం మానేసినప్పుడు ఆ దేశ ప్రభుత్వం తీసుకునే నిర్ణయాలే ఆ దేశ ప్రజలు అనుభవించాల్సి వస్తుంది. యుద్ధమే జరిగితే మన దేశం ఎంత ఆర్థికంగా వెనుకబదుతుందో ఎంతమంది సాధారణ ప్రజల జీవితాలు ప్రభావితం అవుతాయో ఎవరికీ, ఎవ్వరికీ అవసరం లేదు అక్కర లేదు.
ఇప్పుడిప్పుడే మనం ఆర్థికంగా ముందుకి వెళ్తున్నాం యుద్ధం చేస్కుంటూ ఉంటే మిగతా దేశాలు వేడుక చూస్తూ వాళ్ళ దేశాలు ఇంకా ముందుకి వెళ్లిపోతాయి. మనం వెనక పొడిపోతాం. ఎవరూ ఈ అంశం గురించి మాట్లాడట్లేదు. ఆ దేశం పాకిస్తాన్ లో అయినా మన దేశం లో అయినా చచ్చేది ఆర్మీ, సాధారణ ప్రజలు. పాకిస్థాన్ గవర్నమెంట్ పై అన్ని దేశాలు కలిసి ఒత్తిడి తేవాలి. ఆ దేశ ఉగ్రవాదాన్ని ఆ దేశంలోనే అనిచేలా ఇండియన్ ఆర్మీని అనుమతించాలి. అలా ఏదైనా ప్లాన్ ఆలోచించి ఎన్ని రకాలుగా ట్రై చేేయచ్చు అని వీడియోస్ చేసి అవగాహన కల్పిస్తే బాగుంటుంది. ఒకొక్కడు వీడియోలు చేసి పెడుతున్నాడు ఎవరు ఎక్కడ ఎం చేయబోతున్నారో మన దగ్గర ఎంత సామర్థ్యం ఉందో అన్ని ముందే చెప్పేస్తున్నారు. ఏం రోగం రా మీకు views కోసం ఇంత దరిద్రంగా తయారయ్యారు. 
మతాన్ని నమ్ముకొని బతికే దేశాలు ఎప్పుడూ బాగుపడవు ఒకర్ని బాగుపడనియ్యవు.... మతం కులం కంటికి కనపడకుండా మన మెదడులో బతికే ఈ నమ్మకాలను వదిలి బయట పడగలిగితే అందరూ సంతోషంగా బ్రతకగలరు.

Dear Pravasthi !                                                                                                                                                                                                        Don’t let a biased judgment drown out the song your soul was born to sing.                                                                                                  Remember, Lata Mangeshkar was once told her voice was "too thin." Yet she went on to become the Nightingale of India, touching hearts across generations.
Even A.R. Rahman lost his father at a young age and faced deep personal struggles. But through pain, he found purpose—and gave the world music that transcends borders.
Do you know that Kailash Kher was rejected by multiple music directors for not having a 'conventional voice.' Today, that raw, soulful voice has become a national treasure.
When Amitabh Bachchan was rejected by All India Radio for his voice, who would’ve thought that same voice would go on to narrate India's most iconic films?
These legends didn’t wait for validation from a judge’s scorecard. They turned rejection into redirection. They turned pain into power. Your voice is not up for their approval—it is a calling. And that calling doesn’t retire just because one room couldn’t hear your truth.
Don’t let them write your story. Keep singing. Let your voice reach places their judgment never could.


Pravasthi !  "Judges may have missed your brilliance, but the universe never does. Real talent always finds its audience. Keep going."  
God Bless You
